&dhttp.ServerConfig{\\n228: \\t\\tHandler: grpcServer,\\n229: \\t}\\n230: \\treturn sc.Serve(ctx, lis)\\n231: }\\n232: \\n233: // Decoders for unmarshalling our config\\n234: var decoders = map[string](func([]byte, proto.Message) error){\\n235: \\t\\\".json\\\": protojson.Unmarshal,\\n236: \\t\\\".pb\\\":   prototext.Unmarshal,\\n237: }\\n238: \\n239: func isDecodable(name string) bool {\\n240: \\tif strings.HasPrefix(name, \\\".\\\") {\\n241: \\t\\treturn false\\n242: \\t}\\n243: \\n244: \\text := filepath.Ext(name)\\n245: \\t_, ok := decoders[ext]\\n246: \\treturn ok\\n247: }\\n248: \\n249: // Not sure if there is a better way to do this, but we cast to this\\n250: // so we can call the generated Validate method.\\n251: type Validatable interface {\\n252: \\tproto.Message\\n253: \\tValidate() error\\n254: }\\n255: \\n256: func Decode(ctx context.Context, name string) (proto.Message, error) {\\n257: \\tany := &anypb.Any{}\\n258: \\tcontents, err := ioutil.ReadFile(name)\\n259: \\tif err != nil {\\n260: \\t\\treturn nil, err\\n261: \\t}\\n262: \\n263: \\text := filepath.Ext(name)\\n264: \\tdecoder := decoders[ext]\\n265: \\terr = \\t}\\n274: \\n275: \\tv := m.(Validatable)\\n276: \\n277: \\tif err := v.Validate(); err != nil {\\n278: \\t\\treturn nil, err\\n279: \\t}\\n280: \\tdlog.Infof(ctx, \\\"Loaded file %s\\\", name)\\n281: \\treturn v, nil\\n282: }\\n283: \\n284: // Observability:\\n285: //\\n286: // These \\\"expanded\\\" snapshots make the snapshots we log easier to read: basically,\\n287: // instead of just indexing by Golang types, make the JSON marshal with real names.\\n288: type v3ExpandedSnapshot struct {\\n289: \\tEndpoints ecp_v3_cache.Resources `json:\\\"endpoints\\\"`\\n290: \\tClusters and V3 snapshot, for logging.\\n307: type combinedSnapshot struct {\\n308: \\tVersion string             `json:\\\"version\\\"`\\n309: \\tV3      v3ExpandedSnapshot `json:\\\"v3\\\"`\\n310: }\\n311: \\n312: // csDump creates a combinedSnapshot from a V2 snapshot and a V3 snapshot, then\\n313: // dumps the combinedSnapshot to disk. Only numsnaps snapshots are kept: ambex-1.json\\n314: // is the newest, then ambex-2.json, etc., so ambex-$numsnaps.json is the oldest.\\n315: // Every time we write a new one, we rename all the older ones, ditching the oldest\\n316: // after we've written numsnaps snapshots.\\n317: func csDump(ctx context.Context, snapdirPath string, numsnaps int, generation int, v3snap *ecp_v3_cache.Snapshot) {\\n318: \\tif numsnaps <= 0 {\\n319: \\t\\t// Don't do snapshotting at all.\\n320: \\t\\treturn\\n321: \\t}\\n322: \\n323: \\t// OK, they want snapshots. Make a proper version string...\\n324: \\tversion := fmt.Sprintf(\\\"v%d\\\", generation)\\n325: \\n326: \\t// ...and a combinedSnapshot.\\n327: \\tcs := combinedSnapshot{\\n328: \\t\\tVersion: version,\\n329: \\t\\tV3:      NewV3ExpandedSnapshot(v3snap),\\n330: \\t}\\n331: \\n332: \\t// Next up, marshal as JSON and write to ambex-0.json. Note that we\\n333: \\t// didn't say anything about a -0 file; that's because it's about to\\n334: \\t// be renamed.\\n335: \\n336: \\tbs, err := json.MarshalIndent(cs, \\\"\\\", \\\"  \\\")\\n337: \\n338: \\tif err != nil {\\n339: \\t\\tdlog.Errorf(ctx, \\\"CSNAP: marshal failure: %s\\\", err)\\n340: \\t\\treturn\\n341: \\t}\\n342: \\n343: \\tcsPath := path.Join(snapdirPath, \\\"ambex-0.json\\\")\\n344: \\n345: \\terr = ioutil.WriteFile(csPath, bs, 0644)\\n346: \\n347: \\tif err != nil {\\n348: \\t\\tdlog.Errorf(ctx, \\\"CSNAP: write failure: %s\\\", err)\\n349: \\t} else {\\n350: \\t\\tdlog.Infof(ctx, \\\"Saved snapshot %s\\\", version)\\n351: \\t}\\n352: \\n353: \\t// Rotate everything one file down. This includes renaming the just-written\\n354: \\t// ambex-0 to ambex-1.\\n355: \\tfor i := numsnaps; i > 0; i-- {\\n356: \\t\\tprevious := i - 1\\n357: \\n358: \\t\\tfromPath := path.Join(snapdirPath, fmt.Sprintf(\\\"ambex-%d.json\\\", previous))\\n359: \\t\\ttoPath := path.Join(snapdirPath, fmt.Sprintf(\\\"ambex-%d.json\\\", i))\\n360: \\n361: \\t\\terr := os.Rename(fromPath, toPath)\\n362: \\n363: \\t\\tif (err != nil) && !os.IsNotExist(err) {\\n364: \\t\\t\\tdlog.Infof(ctx, \\\"CSNAP: could not rename %s -> %s: %#v\\\", fromPath, toPath, err)\\n365: \\t\\t}\\n366: \\t}\\n367: }\\n368: \\n369: // Get an updated snapshot going.\\n370: func update(\\n371: \\tctx context.Context,\\n372: \\tsnapdirPath string,\\n373: \\tnumsnaps int,\\n374: \\tedsBypass bool,\\n375: \\tconfigv3 ecp_v3_cache.SnapshotCache,\\n376: \\tgeneration *int,\\n377: \\tdirs []string,\\n378: \\tedsEndpointsV3 \\truntimesv3 := []ecp_cache_types.Resource{}  // v3.Runtime\\n387: \\n388: \\tvar filenames []string\\n389: \\n390: \\tfor _, dir := range dirs {\\n391: \\t\\tfiles, err := ioutil.ReadDir(dir)\\n392: := range filenames {\\n405: \\t\\tm, e := Decode(ctx, name)\\n406: \\t\\tif e != nil {\\n407: \\t\\t\\tdlog.Warnf(ctx, \\\"%s: %v\\\", name, e)\\n408: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n409: \\t\\t}\\n410: \\t\\tvar RouteConfiguration is embedded in the listener, it will cause envoy to\\n425: \\t\\t\\t\\t// go through a complete drain cycle whenever there is a routing change and that\\n426: \\t\\t\\t\\t// will potentially disrupt in-flight requests. By converting all listeners to use\\n427: \\t\\t\\t\\t// RDS rather than inlining their routing configuration, we significantly reduce the\\n428: \\t\\t\\t\\t// set of circumstances where the listener definition itself changes, and this in\\n429: \\t\\t\\t\\t// turn reduces the set of circumstances where envoy has to go through that drain\\n430: \\t\\t\\t\\t// process and disrupt in-flight range fastpathSnapshot.Snapshot.Resources[ecp_cache_types.Cluster].Items {\\n462: \\t\\t\\tclustersv3 = append(clustersv3, clu.Resource)\\n463: \\t\\t}\\n464: \\t\\t// We intentionally omit endpoints since those are carried separately.\\n465: \\t}\\n466: \\n467: \\t// The configuration data that reaches us here arrives via two parallel paths that race each\\n468: \\t// other. The endpoint data comes in realtime directly from the golang watcher in the entrypoint\\n469: \\t// package. The cluster configuration comes from the python code. Either one can win which means\\n470: \\t// we might at times see endpoint data with no corresponding cluster and we might also see\\n471: \\t// clusters with no corresponding endpoint data. Both of these circumstances should be\\n472: \\t// transient.\\n473: \\t//\\n474: \\t// To produce a consistent configuration we do an outer join operation on the endpoint and\\n475: \\t// cluster configuration that we have at this moment. If there is no endpoint information for a\\n476: \\t// given cluster, we will synthesize an empty ClusterLoadAssignment.\\n477: \\t//\\n478: \\t// Note that a cluster not existing is very different to envoy than a cluster existing but\\n479: \\t// having an empty ClusterLoadAssignment. When envoy first discovers clusters it goes through a\\n480: \\t// warmup process to be sure the cluster is properly bootstrapped before routing traffic to\\n481: \\t// it. See here for more details:\\n482: \\t//\\n483: \\t// https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/intro/arch_overview/upstream/cluster_manager.html?highlight=cluster%20warming\\n484: \\t//\\n485: \\t// For this reason if there is no endpoint data for the cluster we will synthesize an empty\\n486: \\t// ClusterLoadAssignment rather than filtering out the cluster. This avoids triggering the\\n487: \\t// warmup sequence in scenarios where the endpoint data for a cluster is really flapping into\\n488: \\t// and out of existence. block when it writes to the channel. We therefore need a\\n664: \\t// nonzero buffer for the channel to minimize the possiblity that we miss out on a signal that\\n665: \\t// comes in while we are doing work and not reading from the channel. To minimize the chance\\n666: \\t// of that happening we will choose a buffer size of 100. path.Join(snapdirPath, fmt.Sprintf(\\\"ambex-%d.json\\\", previous))\\n359: \\t\\ttoPath := path.Join(snapdirPath, fmt.Sprintf(\\\"ambex-%d.json\\\", i))\\n360: \\n361: \\t\\terr := os.Rename(fromPath, toPath)\\n362: \\n363: \\t\\tif (err != nil) && !os.IsNotExist(err) {\\n364: \\t\\t\\tdlog.Infof(ctx, \\\"CSNAP: could not rename %s -> %s: %#v\\\", fromPath, toPath, err)\\n365: \\t\\t}\\n366: \\t}\\n367: }\\n368: \\n369: // Get an updated snapshot going.\\n370: func update(\\n371: \\tctx context.Context,\\n372: \\tsnapdirPath string,\\n373: \\tnumsnaps int,\\n374: By converting all listeners to use\\n427: \\t\\t\\t\\t// RDS rather than inlining their routing configuration, we significantly reduce the\\n428: \\t\\t\\t\\t// set of circumstances where the listener definition itself changes, and this in\\n429: \\t\\t\\t\\t// turn reduces the set of circumstances where envoy has to go through that drain\\n430: \\t\\t\\t\\t// process and disrupt in-flight The endpoint data comes in realtime directly from the golang watcher in the entrypoint\\n469: \\t// package. The cluster configuration comes from the python code. Either one can win which means\\n470: \\t// we might at times see endpoint data with no corresponding cluster and we might also see\\n471: \\t// clusters with no corresponding endpoint data. If there is no endpoint information for a\\n476: \\t// given cluster, we will synthesize an empty ClusterLoadAssignment.\\n477: \\t//\\n478: \\t// Note that a cluster not existing is very different to envoy than a cluster existing but\\n479: \\t// having an empty ClusterLoadAssignment. block when it writes to the channel. We therefore need a\\n664: \\t// nonzero buffer for the channel to minimize the possiblity that we miss out on a signal that\\n665: \\t// comes in while we are doing work and not reading from the channel. The root of the world is a SnapshotCache.\n11:  *   - import github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/pkg/cache/v3, then refer\n12:  *     to cache.SnapshotCache.\n13:  *   - A collection of internally consistent configuration objects is a\n14:  *     Snapshot (cache.Snapshot).\n15:  *   - Snapshots are collected in the SnapshotCache.\n16:  *   - A given SnapshotCache can hold configurations for multiple Envoys,\n17:  *     identified by the Envoy 'node ID', which must be configured for the\n18:  *     Envoy.\n19:  * - The SnapshotCache can only hold go-control-plane configuration objects,\n20:  *   so you have to build these up to hand to the SnapshotCache.\n21:  * - The gRPC stuff is handled by a Server.\n22:  *   - import github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/pkg/server, then refer\n23:  *     to server.Server.\n24:  *   - Our runManagementServer (largely ripped off from the go-control-plane\n25:  *     tests) gets this running. It takes a SnapshotCache (cleverly called a\n26:  *     \"config\" for no reason I understand) and a gRPCServer as arguments.\n27:  *   - _ALL_ the gRPC madness is handled by the Server, with the assistance\n28:  *     of the methods in a callback object.\n29:  * - Once the Server is running, Envoy can open a gRPC stream to it.\n30:  *   - On connection, Envoy will get handed the most recent Snapshot that\n31:  *     the Server's SnapshotCache knows about.\n32:  *   - Whenever a newer Snapshot is added to the SnapshotCache, that Snapshot\n33:  *     will get sent to the Envoy.\n34:  * - We manage the SnapshotCache by loading envoy configuration from\n35:  *   json and/or protobuf files on disk.\n36:  *   - By default when we get a SIGHUP, we reload configuration.\n37:  *   - When passed the -watch argument we reload whenever any file in\n38:  *     the directory changes.\n39:  */\n40: \n41: import (\n42: \t// standard library\n43: \t\"context\"\n44: \t\"encoding/json\"\n45: Only numsnaps snapshots are kept: ambex-1.json\n314: // is the newest, then ambex-2.json, etc., so ambex-$numsnaps.json is the oldest.\n315: // Every time we write a new one, we rename all the older ones, ditching the oldest\n316: // after we've written numsnaps snapshots.\n317: func csDump(ctx context.Context, snapdirPath string, numsnaps int, generation int, v3snap *ecp_v3_cache.Snapshot) {\n318: \tif numsnaps <= 0 {\n319: \t\t// Don't do snapshotting at all.\n320: \t\treturn\n321: \t}\n322: \n323: \t// OK, they want snapshots. Make a proper version string...\n324: \tversion := fmt.Sprintf(\"v%d\", generation)\n325: \n326: \t// ...and a combinedSnapshot.\n327: \tcs := combinedSnapshot{\n328: \t\tVersion: version,\n329: \t\tV3:      NewV3ExpandedSnapshot(v3snap),\n330: \t}\n331: \n332: \t// Next up, marshal as JSON and write to ambex-0.json. Note that we\n333: \t// didn't say anything about a -0 file; that's because it's about to\n334: \t// be renamed.\n335: \n336: \tbs, err := json.MarshalIndent(cs, \"\", \"  \")\n337: \n338: \tif err != nil {\n339: \t\tdlog.Errorf(ctx, \"CSNAP: marshal failure: %s\", err)\n340: \t\treturn\n341: \t}\n342: \n343: \tcsPath := path.Join(snapdirPath, \"ambex-0.json\")\n344: \n345: \terr = ioutil.WriteFile(csPath, bs, 0644)\n346: \n347: \tif err != nil {\n348: \t\tdlog.Errorf(ctx, \"CSNAP: write failure: %s\", err)\n349: \t} else {\n350: \t\tdlog.Infof(ctx, \"Saved snapshot %s\", version)\n351: \t}\n352: \n353: \t// Rotate everything one file down. This includes renaming the just-written\n354: \t// ambex-0 to ambex-1.\n355: \tfor i := numsnaps; i > 0; i-- {\n356: \t\tprevious := i - 1\n357: \n358: \t\tfromPath := path.Join(snapdirPath, fmt.Sprintf(\"ambex-%d.json\", previous))\n359: \t\ttoPath := path.Join(snapdirPath, fmt.Sprintf(\"ambex-%d.json\", i))\n360: \n361: \t\terr := os.Rename(fromPath, toPath)\n362: \n363: \t\tif (err != nil) && !os.IsNotExist(err) {\n364: \t\t\tdlog.Infof(ctx, \"CSNAP: could not rename %s -> %s: %#v\", fromPath, toPath, err)\n365: \t\t}\n366: \t}\n367: }\n368: \n369: // Get an updated snapshot going.\n370: func update(\n371: \tctx context.Context,\n372: \tsnapdirPath string,\n373: \tnumsnaps int,\n374: \tedsBypass bool,\n375: \tconfigv3 ecp_v3_cache.SnapshotCache,\n376: \tgeneration
